Razi's Second Proof Against the Possibility of Existence
Razi presents the second proof that imkan cannot be an attribute.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Imam Razi's second proof that the concept of 'imkan' (possibility of existence) leads to a logical contradiction, thus cannot be a real attribute.

Core Idea
Possibility cannot exist nor be non-existent—so it is impossible.

Imam Razi is systematically dismantling the notion that things can be 'possible of existence' in themselves. In this second proof, he uses a dichotomy: if something is possible, its possibility must either exist or not exist. Both options lead to absurdities, showing that the very concept of imkan is self-contradictory. This lesson walks through Razi's reasoning step by step.

Guided Path
1
Understand the question
Razi asks: if something is possible, is its possibility (imkan) itself existent or non-existent? Notice the dichotomy.
2
Examine each option
First, imkan cannot be existent (already refuted). Second, it cannot be non-existent because removal of impossibility is affirmative (thubuti).
3
Reach the conclusion
Since both divisions are invalid, the statement that something is possible of existence is false.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الحجة الثانية : أنا لو فرضنا شيئًا من الأشياء ممكن الوجود لكان ذلك الإمكان إما أن يكون موجودًا أو معدومًا، لا جائز أن يكون موجودًا للوجوه الكثيرة التي ذكرناها في الجواب عن شبه الفلاسفة في قدم الأجسام، ولا جائز أن يكون معدوماً ؛ لأن الشيء بتقدير أن يكون ممكن الوجود كان موصوفًا في نفسه بالإمكان، وذلك الإمكان رافع للامتناع والامتناع عدم ورفع العدم ثبوت، فوجب أن يكون الإمكان أمرًا ثبوتيًا، ولما كان القول بكون الشيء ممكن الوجود يقتضي أن يكون الإمكان إما أن يكون وصفا سلبيًا أو وصفًا وجوديًا، وكان القسمان باطلين فكان القول يكون الشيء ممكن الوجود باطلا.
The second proof: If we suppose something from among things to be possible of existence, then that possibility (al-imkan) would either be existent or non-existent. It cannot be existent due to the many considerations we mentioned in the response to the philosophers' doubts about the pre-eternity of bodies. And it cannot be non-existent, because when a thing is supposed to be possible of existence, it is described in itself with possibility, and that possibility removes impossibility; impossibility is non-existence, and the removal of non-existence is affirmation, so possibility must be an affirmative thing. And since the statement that something is possible of existence requires that possibility be either a negative attribute or an existential attribute, and both divisions are invalid, then the statement that something is possible of existence is false.
Source pages p. 89

Commentary
This passage is a proof (al-hujja al-thaniya) against the coherence of 'imkan' as an attribute. Razi supposes something is possible of existence, then asks: is the imkan itself existent or non-existent? It cannot be existent due to earlier reasons. It also cannot be non-existent because imkan removes impossibility, and removing non-existence is affirmative (thubuti). Thus imkan must be thubuti, but then it would be an existential attribute, leading to the earlier problem. Both options are invalid, so the notion of something being 'possible of existence' is false.

Key Terms
إمكان
ثبوتي
وصف سلبي
وصف وجودي

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Many assume that 'imkan' (possibility) is a straightforward, simple concept that can be attributed to things.
Correction: Razi shows that on analysis, 'imkan' leads to contradictions: if it is existent, it is subject to the same problems; if non-existent, it cannot remove impossibility since removal of non-existence is affirmative. Thus 'imkan' is not a coherent attribute.

Checkpoint
According to Razi's second argument, if something is possible of existence, its possibility (imkan) must be either existent or non-existent. Why can it not be non-existent?
A) Because non-existence cannot be described as possibility
B) Because possibility removes impossibility, and removal of non-existence is affirmative (thubuti)
C) Because the philosophers already proved it
D) Because non-existence is not a real attribute

Key Takeaway
Razi's second proof shows that the concept of imkan (possibility) is self-contradictory: it cannot be existent nor non-existent, so the notion that something can be 'possible of existence' is false.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
You have just seen that the very concept of 'possible existence' leads to self-contradiction. If your own existence is not truly 'possible' in any real sense, then on what do you base your hope for tomorrow? Do you rely on abstract possibilities, or do you anchor your trust in the One whose existence is necessary?
?
When you consider your own life, you typically think, 'I could be this or that.' But if Razi is right, such possibilities are not real attributes. What does that mean for the way you view your choices and your future? Will you continue to live as if possibilities are real, or will you submit to the reality that only Allah's will and power are truly effective?
?
Razi argues that possibility cannot be affirmed because it leads to contradictory positions. How often do you hold onto beliefs or plans without examining their foundations? Are you willing to let go of comfortable but ultimately incoherent ideas about your own capabilities and instead rely entirely on the Necessary Being?

Allah's Existence
advanced
5 min
Razi's Third Argument: Possibility Implies Non-Existent as a Thing
Opening segment of Razi's third proof: possibility requires non-existent to be a thing.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Razi's argument that the concept of possibility (imkan) necessarily implies that the non-existent is a determinable thing, which opposes the school that denies the non-existent is a thing.

Core Idea
Possibility forces the non-existent to be something.

Razi presents his third argument against the possibility of existence. He begins by showing that if something can be described as possible to exist or not exist, then that thing must be determined in itself even when non-existent. This leads to the conclusion that the non-existent is a thing—a position his opponents reject. Let's trace his reasoning.

Guided Path
1
Read the first part of the argument
Read the Arabic passage up to 'وأنتم لا تقولون به' and its translation. Notice the conditional structure: if possibility, then determination in non-existence, then implies non-existent is a thing.
Focus on the logical chain: جواز العدم → تقرر → كون المعدوم شيئًا.
2
Identify the opponent's position
Razi ends this section by stating 'وأنتم لا تقولون به' (and you do not hold that). Recognize that his opponents reject the notion that the non-existent is a thing, so this argument forces them to abandon possibility as well.
3
Reflect on the implication
Consider why the opponent cannot accept the conclusion. If they accept that possibility implies the non-existent is a thing, they would have to revise their ontology. But since they do not, possibility becomes incoherent.
This is a reductio ad absurdum style argument.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الحجة الثالثة: أنا إذا قلنا الشيء يجوز أن يكون موجودا، ويجوز أن يكون معدوما يقتضي تقرر ذلك الشيء حال وصفه بكونه معدوما، وهذا يقتضي كون المعدوم شيئًا، وأنتم لا تقولون به. وأيضا : القائل بأن المعدوم شيء لا يمكنه القول بالإمكان؛ وذلك لأن الإمكان على هذا التقدير إما أن يكون وصفًا للماهية أو وصفًا للوجود ولا جائز أن يكون وصفًا للماهية ؛ لأن الماهية يستحيل عليها الانقلاب والتغير، فلا يعقل كون الإمكان وصفًا لها، ولا جائز أن يكون وصفًا للوجود لأن الوجود قبل تجدده وحدوثه ما كان ثابتا ولا متعينا والإمكان عندكم ثابت قبل الحدوث، وإذا كان كذلك امتنع القول بجعل الإمكان صفة للوجود.
The third proof: When we say that something can be existent and can be non-existent, this necessitates that thing being determined while described as non-existent, and this necessitates that the non-existent is a thing, and you (opponents) do not hold that. Also, whoever says that the non-existent is a thing cannot hold possibility (al-imkan), because possibility on this account is either an attribute of the essence (mahiyya) or an attribute of existence. It cannot be an attribute of the essence because the essence cannot undergo change and alteration, so it is not conceivable that possibility be an attribute of it. And it cannot be an attribute of existence because existence before its renewal and coming-to-be was not established nor determined, while possibility in your view is established before coming-to-be. Since this is so, the statement that possibility is an attribute of existence is precluded.
Source pages p. 89

Commentary
This passage is a third proof against imkan. Razi argues that saying something is possible requires the thing to be determined even when non-existent, implying the non-existent is a thing – which opponents deny. He then turns to those who accept the non-existent is a thing: they still cannot hold imkan because it would be an attribute of either the essence (mahiyya) or existence. Essences are immutable, so imkan cannot be an attribute of them. Existence does not exist before it comes to be, while imkan is posited before existence. Thus imkan is impossible.

Key Terms
معدوم
تقرر

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Possibility is a neutral attribute that does not commit one to any ontological claim about the non-existent.
Correction: Razi shows that saying 'x can be non-existent' requires x to be determined in non-existence, which implies x is a thing even when non-existent. Thus possibility presupposes that the non-existent is something.

Checkpoint
According to Razi's third argument, what does the statement 'something can be existent and can be non-existent' necessarily imply?
A) That the thing is eternal.
B) That the thing is determined (مقرر) while non-existent.
C) That the thing is impossible.
D) That the thing is a substance.

Key Takeaway
Razi's first step: possibility entails that the non-existent is a thing, which his opponents deny, so they must abandon possibility.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you say 'I could have chosen otherwise,' do you treat that potential choice as something real? What does Razi's argument uncover about your hidden assumptions?
?
If the non-existent is not a thing, then your past possibilities—your roads not taken—are nothing. Can you live with that nothingness, or do you feel compelled to grant them some reality?
?
Razi forces you to choose: either reject possibility or accept that non-existence has a kind of reality. Which do you choose, and why does it matter to your view of God's power?
